<rate>1</rate>< review>
This place is horrible. Open showers, dirty bathrooms, food trucks, Shopette lines are ridiculously long and you'll wait for sure about 45 minutes in some cases. I'd rather go back to Iraq. It was cold as hell when I went to the box and the OC's didn't let us grab our cold weather gear. It was awful. Be ready to bring everything with you while you're fighting OPFOR specially when it's winter time. Fortunately time flights fast and you'll be out of here before you even know it. I recommend you hiding your phone though. Just use it in case of an emergency because remember you're literally alone in the desert.<//review>

<UserId.>110165636728385229613</UserId.><name>EXPRECDJ<//name><Time>1496678556410<//Time>< rating>
4<//rating>
<Review>The Army's premier training center for Brigade sized mechanized and heavy infantry movements and maneuvers. Tent city includes insulation and air conditioning, latrines were fine, but the PX shopette was completely overrun and not capable of handling 4000+ soldiers. It was always packed and ridiculously long lines.

Units never bring enough water, so make sure to buy a case of water each day and load up on at a months supply of baby wipes and field supplies before heading to the 'box'. The heat and sun and brutal, it's literally the Mojave desert and temperatures reach well over 100 degrees, no shade anywhere to be found, plus a 40 degree drop in temperature overnight.

The base itself is beautiful, great California style base housing and apartments, plenty of MWR facilities and a brand new hospital. The scenery is surreal, breathtaking mountains and dune type sands. The main PX is relatively smaller but well stocked and organized. Everything is within about a mile walking distance from the NTC Rotational Unit barracks area.

All in all, great memories here.< /Review><Pics>None</Pics>< resp>
None< /resp>

<resp>None< /resp><user_id>107442718832767540337<//user_id>< review>
My having served a 2 yr deployment as an OPFOR medic in Irwin 04-06,  my advice is to, maintain your game soldiers.  Attention to detail, teamwork is the key,  use this opportunity to save up money.  You will have everything you need to get by.  Although the field rotations can be taxing, they are lessons leaned you can apply toward your future careers.  In addition use the doggone gym, and maximize the resources from the library on post by living simply, saving up your LES's for future investments, you can make the most of your time at the sandbox hooah.  Respectfully, Veteran Field Medic SGT John Knott  radio callsign "Highlander Medic" reporting in<//review>

< username>
Drew</username>

1374766548611</Time>
< Rating>
5<//Rating>
<review>Looking back, I loved this post. Better mounted maneuver training than you'll get anywhere else in the Army. The OPTEMPO sucks, so its tough for families while you're out in the box. Almost always sunny- hot but dry so its not bad. The post itself is austere, but pretty nice. Its got all the necessities- good housing, a nice town center (two starbucks!), some decent restaurants (pizza hut, subway, BK, KFC, the usual PX restaurants and Sam Adams), and some really nice parks for the kids. That being said, its a long way from everything else- so once again, it's hard on families. Though you're along way from everything- your within driving distance to some great vacations- San Diego (2-3 hrs), Las Vegas (2-3 hrs), San Francisco (maybe 6-7 hours), Yosemite (6-8 hours), LA (3 hrs), Big Bear (2 hrs)... etc.

If given the opportunity, I'd go back.</review><pictures>None<//pictures>< response>
None<//response>
<GmapID>0x80c43a64657c8eb5:0xc8482366a158e859<//GmapID></record>
</dataset><record>
<name>Chad Jackson< /name><UserId.>117282454770383703596< /UserId.>< text>
In terms of training our Army and other services, Fort Irwin is an exceptional location.  There are not many places in the US where a brigade-sized unit can conduct training.  This is the place where all the individual and unit training culminates in preparation to continue on to combat missions.  The National Training Center and Fort Irwin are uniquely equipped to help unit better improve themselves.

As for being stationed here, you are in a gated community at the end of the worlds longest cul-de-sac.  You are over 30 miles from the nearest "civilization" in Barstow, but most will bypass Barstow to go to Victorville for most of their needs not provided on the post itself.  Fort Irwin does have a fairly nice PX and Commissary, and housing has seen drastic, positive changes the past 10 years.  Homes are a tad small, but are very nice.  I think most families that are stationed here actually like it.  If you are single, you will probably have issues, but hey, Vegas is only 3 hours away.<//text>

< Text>
While Brian, Coco and Fari are as nice as can be, please think twice about leaving you car here for repairs. After my car being in their possession for a month I am forced to file a complaint with the Better Business Bureau as well as the Bureau of Automotive Repair.
Albeit long, here is my story.

They have had my car for 4 weeks now for a repair to pass smog. Against my knowing, they are having it repaired by another shop.

Brought my 1991 VW Vanagon in to Nono's 76 to have it smogged on Sept 8. Was told it will take 25 minutes. 45 minutes later I noticed that people that have come in after me are leaving. Turns out the machine my car was on was bad. Asked the tech about it and he yelled at me and my wife. After an hour and a half, car is done and failed smog.

Upholstery and interior is filthy with grease. Am given a coupon for a car wash.

I am assured by Fari (the supervisor) that they have an expert mechanic who is great with VW vans and that Fari himself had one and has experience working on them. Left it there that day and requested an oil change since it was there anyway. Called to inquire 2 days later and am told that it is done but something has happened during the process that has made the van run poorly. Am asked to test drive it and see for myself. Drive it home and keep it overnight. Car has very little power and is stalling out. Bring it back the next day and talk to Coco who tells me that they weren't even the ones who did the repairs. Ask who did them and he tells me he'll find out. Also tells me that something shorted out while the new catalytic converter was being welded in. They forgot to do the oil change.

Call a couple days later and find out that the car is over at Kartek Mufflers and they are the ones who are working on it. Call a couple times more and speak to Coco who tells me it's not done yet. He eventually hands me back over to Fari who says that Kartek needs an air flow meter and can't find one. Asks me to check to see if I can find one. He might have a lead on a used one. Give him 2 places that have them. 2 days later he tells me they are out of stock. I call that day and find out that that is not true. Fari says that he told his clerk to order it and that's what he told him.

Stop off at Kartek and get their side of the story. Eddie at Kartek tells me that nothing shorted out while they were welding and he just needs the new air flow meter and the car will be fine. Part comes in and I call to see when the van is ready. Eddie tells me that it's done but not running great (which it was when I dropped it off - Drove to San Diego and back without a problem) I take it home for the weekend and the same problem exists. Car has a bit more power but is now hesitating and surging. Stalls again. Bring it back to Eddie and he tells me that he didn't have time to make the needed adjustments on the new air flow meter and wants to call the company where it was purchased to make sure the adjustments won't void the warranty. It is now 3 weeks later.

Call Eddie on Oct 1 (Mind you I have no agreement with Eddie at Kartek to do any repairs. If it were up to me I would have brought it to my VW specialist). Eddie tells me the mechanic who was working on it has not been at work all week because his dog was sick. I am assured that the mechanic is back and will be working on my van and it will be ready on Friday. Call on Friday and am told that they were very busy and that he will definitely have it done on Saturday. Call 3 times on Saturday and am eventually told that they did not get to it and it will be ready on Monday.

Called Fari and explain the situation to him and tell him I'm filing a complaint since I did not authorize this 3rd party to work on the car and after almost 1 month I do not have it. I am seeking a refund to 1. Pay for my rental car for the last month and 2. to pay for my personal mechanic to fix the problem.< /Text>

<rate>5</rate>< text>
Formerly known as, The Good Cup, this cafe got a full on flip my house renovation and it looks good! New owners, new interior, new everything as of 2018. They even carry the town's best local espresso here, Handlebar Coffee, and pastries from the same bakery Handlebar uses. It's now a very beachy, communal style environment with strong wifi, a few scattered outlet options, booths, tables and out door patio seating. The bathrooms are a breath of fresh air too, which, if you knew Good Cup before, is really the cherry on top of this cafe renovation.

While in town I visited a handful of times trying their cucumber toast, oat milk latte, and ac√°i bowls. All a few cents more than I would like to spend but well worth the purchases, would 100% recommend, and will be back for more! Handlebar Coffee, in and of itself, is a gem and the fact that there's a venue on the Mesa that carries it now just raised property values significantly, in my opinion! It's a must try, and oat milk is the best cream to combo it with.

The staff here are all so sweet and hardworking! They make a point to remember so many customer's names and keep things personable in a professional manner. They are super knowledgable on the brand and get things done in a prompt manner. I have nothing but great things to say about the food, drinks, and staff here. Oh and they're pet friendly (outside) so there's usually really awesome dogs hanging out nearby.

The parking lot seems to always have some construction going on and is definitely not ideal to find a spot quickly around lunch or dinner time. Lazy Acres, the amazing grocery store, is right across the lot + CVS and a hair salon are right next door the the cafe. Lighthouse brings a well fitting, super chill vibe to the Mesa in a modern fashion that fits the community perfectly and is well worth a visit.<//text>

<user_id>114345246665976579548< /user_id><user_name>House Cyril< /user_name>< date>
1582026041880<//date>
<Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
New favorite coffee shop! The atmosphere is great for studying or catching up with some friends. There are plenty of tables inside and a few outside, but the place can get pretty packed. If you need an outlet to charge, I'd recommend grabbing a table along the wall. There's a very clean bathroom inside, which is a huge perk if you plan to stay here for a few hours!

I've tried their Iced Chai with Almond Milk, Iced Latte with Almond Milk, and Cucumber Toast. All were delicious and I love that they have a variety of non-dairy milk options (soy, almond, oat). They also have a case of pastries featuring some local artisanal donuts from Hook and Press!

One thing to keep in mind if you're trying to reduce your single-use plastic: bring your own cup for all iced drinks! Unfortunately, they only have plastic cups which they use for "for here" orders. The smallest size for the iced drinks is 16oz, so make sure to bring a large enough cup. I brought my own cup the second time I came and saved $0.25!!! Save money and save the earth while sipping on some delicious drinks :)</Review>

<review>We stayed here for just one night on our anniversary.   This is a charming boutique hotel just a block away from the main shopping areas  and restaurants in Solvang.  The owners of the hotel also own the Coquelicot winery in Los Olivos and we were please to receive a complementary bottle of wine in our room along with a coupon for a free wine tasting at their winery in Los Olivos, just 15 minutes away from the hotel.   We took advantage of the free wine tasting which was well worth the trip to Los Olivos.   Highly recommend making the trip.   There a many wineries and tasting rooms and the town itself is very quaint.   All in all, a wonderful, romantic stay and we enjoyed the hotel.   The only complaint is that our room was above the restaurant and they were playing music at 7 am which I think is too early.   The walls are pretty thin so you can here music and people talking in the restaurant at night too, but things were quiet after 10 PM.   No big deal.< /review>< response>
None<//response>

We enjoyed our stay, the staff is very friendly and helpful, taking every precaution to ensure our stay was a safe one. Our room was very clean, comfortable and cozy with a lovely fireplace. There is "First and Oak" the Michelin stared restaurant on site which is very convenient after walking through the village all day, you definitely want to make reservations. It is perfectly located and in the heart of all the action which was nice. You can hear people in the surrounding rooms as well as in the lobby, but everything quiets down in the evening. We enjoyed ourselves immensely and our stay here was a cherry on top. We would highly recommend this great little spot and look forward to staying again.</review>

<text>This is a very pretty property with a wonderful location. It is right down the street from all the shops/restaurants/tasting rooms in Solvang. Their First and Oak restaurant located on the property was delicious and definitely worth a reservation. The perks of the wine bottle in the room and the free wine tasting in Los Olivos was awesome. The staff was friendly, and the bed was very comfortable. That being said, there were definitely issues. First of all, in this time of Covid, we were told we would have our temperature taken on arrival and be given our own hand sanitizer. Upon arrival, I only had to answer two questions, both asking if I've been to China lately. Really? The room was spacious, and had a lot of room to put a mini fridge, a coffee maker, but it had neither one of those items. We had to go downstairs to get coffee in the morning. I drink hot lemon water in the mornings instead of coffee. They could give us hot water, but even though they have a restaurant attached to them, they couldn't give me a lemon. It is a lovely older building that has some updates. Our biggest disappointment was that our room, #3, was not quiet!  We were at the top of the stairs and you could hear all conversations in the small lobby area at the foot of the stairs, plus some noise from restaurant and breakfast area. The people in the room above us were up talking and moving around all night and with the wood type flooring all the noise was heard. Needless to say, it was not a very restful night. The staff was excellent, the complimentary morning breakfast was above average, and location good. So, if you can live with the noise, a nice place to stay.<//Review>

< Review>
When I walked into Sago Boba Shop I was surprised by its uniqueness. It is unlike any other boba spot I have been to and that is because of the abundance amount of toys, children's books, candy, chips, and drawings laid out on the right side of the establishment's wall. It certainly appeals to families and the place seems nice for children. The worker was helpful and informal, she informed me of the sushi burrito and that it is a special item served only on the weekends.

Their boba was good, nothing extraordinary from what I have tasted. I give their Cookies n Cream smoothie with boba a 4/5 and their Strawberry smoothie with boba a 4/5 as well. It is a good spot nearby.< /Review>

<name>Guillermo Vazquez</name><Time>1588913066680</Time><rate>5<//rate>< Review>
Great customer service! I had sent a message through their site to get a quote on replacing the main sewerline, drainage pipes and waterlines. I wasn't expecting a call till the next business day, but within 10 minutes, I received a phone call.

An appointment was set for a plumber to come by; Brain L. was the guy who came over, he went under the crawlspace to check everything out, addressed my concerns and went over different options.

He was great at explaining everything, what he recommended and didn't try to upsell me unnecessary things. He quoted me a good price for all the work that needed to be done and estimated the entire project to take at least three days.

In the end, it only took a day and half, half the estimated time, so I was impressed with how fast they did all the work. They did great work, cleaned up everything after they were done and answered any questions I had.

I highly recommend Mr. Rooter, and ask for Brain L.

Mr. Rooter, Brain L. deserves a huge raise!

Sidenote: The dispatchers (Tania is the one I spoke to most often) do a wonderful job at communication, they call to let you know when the plumber is on their way, if you don't pick up, they'll leave a voice message AND send you a text if it's a cell number.

I do like that Mr. Rooter utilizes texting as a way of communication with their customers, keeping up with the times.< /Review>
